Each act of transmission in digital networks entails (in the current state of technology and law) several reproductions. This means that there are two rights that apply to digitaltransmissions: the reproduction right and the making available right. This may complicate the licensing of works foronline use notably when the two rights are held by different persons/entities.

Both what and where should be clarified. In regards to protecting copyright, the creator should have the jurisdiction. There are currently too many loop holes and these need to be tightened. 

The country of origin is the location of where the author has made his work available under the conditions of that country. The targeting-option is confusing in that whoever an author or service provider targets, no one can insure that the other potential users have access to the "content". Legal downloading of the content should prevail above the targeting approach

ï‚ YES The scope of the right of making available in cross-border situations is sufficiently clear â€“ particularly in light of the recent jurisprudence of the CJEU. The nature of the right of making available right for copyright works is such that it takes place both where the offer is made and where it is capable of being accessed by consumers. This is important not only to the licensing of content but also to determining the jurisdiction and/or the applicable law forright holdersto enforce their rights against infringers and online intermediaries. ï‚ YES The scope of the right of making available in cross-border situations is sufficiently clear â€“ particularly in light of the recent jurisprudence of the CJEU. The nature of the right of making available right for copyright works is such that it takes place both where the offer is made and where it is capable of being accessed by consumers. This is important not only to the licensing of content but also to determining the jurisdiction and/or the applicable law forright holdersto enforce their rights against infringers and online intermediaries. Consequently the right covers acts taking place not only in the country of origin but everywhere where the access by consumers has an economic effect to the disadvantage of the right holder and the content provider enables such access. â€œStreamingâ€ is a prime example of such accessing of content. ï‚ NOâ€“Pleaseexplain how this could be clarified and what typeofclarification would be required(e.g.as in "targeting" approach explained above,as in "country of origin"approach) ï‚ NO OPINION

Because i am not getting my royalty rights 

An application of the country of origin principle would have negative effect if introduced relating to the â€œmaking availableâ€ or any other exclusive right of copyright, as it would weaken its usefulness. The making available right is most useful when an infringement can be brought against a party who does not make an unauthorised reproduction in a particular territory (but very often) has done so or assisted or facilitated the making of a copy in another jurisdiction. The making available right is also useful in that the exceptions from copyright infringement in relation to the reproduction right are not co-extensive with the exceptions from infringement relatingto the making available right. ï‚ NOâ€“Pleaseexplain how this could be clarified and what typeofclarification would be required(e.g.as in "targeting" approach explained above,as in "country of origin"approach) â€¦â€¦â€¦â€¦â€¦â€¦â€¦â€¦â€¦â€¦â€¦â€¦â€¦â€¦â€¦â€¦â€¦â€¦â€¦â€¦â€¦â€¦â€¦â€¦â€¦â€¦â€¦â€¦â€¦â€¦â€¦â€¦â€¦â€¦â€¦â€¦. â€¦â€¦â€¦â€¦â€¦â€¦â€¦â€¦â€¦â€¦â€¦â€¦â€¦â€¦â€¦â€¦â€¦â€¦â€¦â€¦â€¦â€¦â€¦â€¦â€¦â€¦â€¦â€¦â€¦â€¦â€¦â€¦â€¦â€¦â€¦â€¦. ï‚ NO OPINION
